Extensions\\n110:  * must invoke the lifecycle hooks appropriately.\\n111:  * <p>\\n112:  * This class takes the following approach for sending status updates to the backing store:\\n113:  *\\n114:  * <ol>\\n115:  * <li>\\n116:  *    When the connector or task is starting, we overwrite the previous state blindly. This ensures that\\n117:  *    every rebalance will reset the state of tasks to the proper state. The intuition is that there should\\n118:  *    be less chance of write conflicts when the worker has just received its assignment and is starting tasks.\\n119:  *    In particular, this prevents us from depending on the generation absolutely. If the group disappears\\n120:  *    and the generation is reset, then we'll overwrite the status information with the older (and larger)\\n121:  *    generation with the updated one. The danger of this approach is that slow starting tasks may cause the\\n122:  *    status to be overwritten after a rebalance has completed.\\n123:  *\\n124:  * <li>\\n125:  *    If the connector or task fails or is shutdown, we use {@link StatusBackingStore#putSafe(ConnectorStatus)},\\n126:  *    which provides a little more protection if the worker is no longer in the group (in which case the\\n127:  *    task may have already been started on another worker). Obviously this is still racy. If the task has just\\n128:  *    started on another worker, we may not have the updated status cached yet. In this case, we'll overwrite\\n129:  *    the value which will cause the state to be inconsistent (most likely until the next rebalance). Until\\n130:  *    we have proper producer groups with fenced groups, there is not much else we can do.\\n131:  * </ol>\\n132:  */\\n133: public abstract class AbstractHerder implements Herder,  private final CachedConnectors cachedConnectors;\\n149: \\n150:     public AbstractHerder(Worker worker,\\n151:                           String workerId,\\n152:                           String kafkaClusterId,\\n153:                           StatusBackingStore statusBackingStore,\\n154:                           ConfigBackingStore configBackingStore,\\n155: this;\\n159:         this.workerId = workerId;\\n160:         this.kafkaClusterId = kafkaClusterId;\\n161:         this.statusBackingStore = statusBackingStore;\\n162:         this.configBackingStore = configBackingStore;\\n163:         this.connectorClientConfigOverridePolicyPlugin = Plugin.wrapInstance(\\n164:                 connectorClientConfigOverridePolicy,\\n165: Initialize scheduler\\n- `void shutdown() throws InterruptedException` - Stop all scheduled tasks\\n\\n## Connect Framework Lifecycle\\n\\nKafka Connect implements similar patterns:\\n\\n**Connect** (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/Connect.java:35):\\n- `start()` - comprehensive Startable/Stoppable service lifecycle pattern across its core broker, controller, and Connect components. The pattern is hierarchical and ensures coordinated startup and shutdown of dependent services.\\n\\n## Core Lifecycle Abstraction\\n\\nThe foundation is the `Server` trait (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/Server.scala:27) which defines three key methods:\\n- `startup(): Unit` - Initialize and start the server\\n- `shutdown(): Unit` - Gracefully shutdown the server\\n- `awaitShutdown(): Unit` - Block until shutdown is complete\\n\\n## Startup Chain\\n\\n**KafkaRaftServer (entry point)** -> ControllerServer + BrokerServer:\\nKafkaRaftServer.startup() (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/KafkaRaftServer.scala:90-98) orchestrates startup in the correct order:\\n1. Starts the ControllerServer first (controller endpoints needed for broker)\\n2. Then starts the BrokerServer\\n3. Registers app info and metrics\\n\\n**BrokerServer.startup()** (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/BrokerServer.scala:189) starts in sequence:\\n1. SharedServer.startForBroker() - initializes shared components\\n2. KafkaScheduler.startup() - scheduler for background tasks\\n3. LogManager initialization\\n4. BrokerLifecycleManager creation\\n5. SocketServer creation and configuration\\n6. Replica manager, coordinators, and metadata publishers\\n7. Request handlers startup\\n8. State transitions to STARTED\\n\\n**ControllerServer.startup()** (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/ControllerServer.scala:123) starts:\\n1. Dynamic configuration initialization\\n2. Quota managers\\n3. Metadata cache and publishers (KRaftMetadataCachePublisher, FeaturesPublisher)\\n4. QuorumController instance\\n5. SocketServer for controller APIs\\n6. State transitions to STARTED\\n\\n**SharedServer** (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/SharedServer.scala) manages shared resources:\\n1. startForBroker() or startForController() - coordinate single start\\n2. Creates and starts KafkaRaftManager (core/src/main/scala/kafka/raft/RaftManager.scala)\\n3. KafkaRaftManager.startup() initializes the Raft client and network channel\\n4. MetadataLoader processes metadata updates\\n\\n## Shutdown Sequence (Reverse Order)\\n\\n**KafkaRaftServer.shutdown()** (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/KafkaRaftServer.scala:100-107) orchestrates shutdown:\\n1. Shuts down BrokerServer first (may need controller for controlled shutdown)\\n2. Then shuts down ControllerServer\\n3. Unregisters app info\\n\\n**BrokerServer.shutdown()** (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/BrokerServer.scala:729-820) follows strict sequence:\\n1. Optionally begins controlled shutdown (replicaManager and lifecycleManager)\\n2. Begins shutdown of BrokerLifecycleManager\\n3. Stops socket server request processors\\n4. Metadata publishers cleanup\\n5. Request handler pool shutdown\\n6. Scheduler shutdown (CRITICAL - before LogManager to prevent concurrent operations)\\n7. LogManager shutdown\\n8. ReplicaManager shutdown\\n9. Coordinator shutdown\\n10. Final resource cleanup\\n\\n**ControllerServer.shutdown()** (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/ControllerServer.scala:126) shuts down:\\n1. SocketServer\\n2. QuorumController\\n3. Metadata publishers\\n4. Request handlers\\n5. Quota managers\\n\\n**RaftManager.shutdown()** (core/src/main/scala/kafka/raft/RaftManager.scala:171-179) cleanly closes:\\n1. Expiration service\\n2. Client driver\\n3. Scheduler\\n4. Network channel\\n5. Replicated log\\n6. Data directory locks\\n\\n## Java Scheduler Interface\\n\\nThe `Scheduler` interface (server-common/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/server/util/Scheduler.java:27) defines the pattern:\\n- `void startup()` - Initialize scheduler\\n- `void shutdown() throws InterruptedException` - Stop all scheduled tasks\\n\\n## Connect Framework Lifecycle\\n\\nKafka Connect implements similar patterns:\\n\\n**Connect** (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/Connect.java:35):\\n- `start()` - Starts herder, REST server, and shutdown hook\\n- `stop()` - Stops herder and REST server\\n- `awaitStop()` - Blocks until shutdown complete\\n\\n**Herder** interface (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/Herder.java:63-68):\\n- `void start()` - Start herder\\n- `void stop()` - Stop herder\\n\\n**AbstractHerder** (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/AbstractHerder.java:180-192):\\n- `startServices()` - Starts worker, statusBackingStore, configBackingStore\\n- `stopServices()` - Stops services in reverse order, shuts down executor\\n\\n**Backing Stores** implement consistent lifecycle:\\n- KafkaOffsetBackingStore.start() (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/storage/KafkaOffsetBackingStore.java:231) starts internal offsetLog\\n- KafkaOffsetBackingStore.stop() (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/storage/KafkaOffsetBackingStore.java:260) stops offsetLog\\n- FileOffsetBackingStore implements similar pattern\\n\\n**KafkaBasedLog** (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/util/KafkaBasedLog.java:220-286):\\n- `start()` - Creates producer/consumer, reads to log end, starts work thread\\n- `stop()` - Signals stop, joins thread, closes clients\\n\\n## Key Design Patterns\\n\\n1. **State Machine**: ProcessStatus enum (SHUTDOWN, STARTING, STARTED, SHUTTING_DOWN) with atomic transitions\\n2. **Dependency Ordering**: Strict startup sequence ensures dependencies are ready before dependent components start\\n3. **Reverse Shutdown**: Shutdown follows reverse of startup order to safely close dependent services first\\n4. **Exception Safety**: Uses CoreUtils.swallow() to continue shutdown despite exceptions\\n5. **Locking**: ReentrantLock and condition variables coordinate state transitions and await shutdown\\n6. **Timeouts**: Deadline-based timeouts prevent indefinite blocking during startup/shutdown\\n7. **Coordinated Startup**: SharedServer.startForBroker()/startForController() ensure single initialization of shared components\\n8. **Graceful Shutdown**: Controlled shutdown protocol allows clean hand-off of responsibilities before hard stop\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
